2026-03-15T15:50:58.5313916Z 
2026-03-15T15:50:58.5314287Z When `ComputeDefaultTasks(player)` is called (passing the player/leader):
2026-03-15T15:50:58.5315263Z - The function iterates `m_DefaultPedTaskPairs`
2026-03-15T15:50:58.5316191Z - For each entry, it skips if `ped && tp.Ped != ped` — so it only processes the entry for `ped`
2026-03-15T15:50:58.5316552Z 
2026-03-15T15:50:58.5316556Z 
2026-03-15T15:50:58.5317332Z - This means when we call it with the player, only the task pair where `tp.Ped == player` gets processed, and since the player is the leader, they get assigned the FOLLOW_LEADER_ANY_MEANS task while other gang members get WANDER_GANG.
2026-03-15T15:50:58.5318132Z 
2026-03-15T15:50:58.5319931Z Wait, that doesn't make sense—the player shouldn't be following themselves. Let me look at the actual code more carefully to see what's really happening with the condition checks. I'm realizing the logic is backwards—when `ped` is null, the leader's pair would still skip the FollowLeaderAnyMeans assignment because the condition `ped == leader` would be `nullptr == leader`, which is false. So the leader would get WanderGang instead, which doesn't make sense either.
2026-03-15T15:50:58.5321952Z 
2026-03-15T15:50:58.5322729Z Let me reconsider what's actually happening: the `ped` parameter being passed in determines which specific task assignment logic applies, not which gang member is being processed.
2026-03-15T15:50:58.5323501Z 
2026-03-15T15:50:58.5329045Z When `ComputeDefaultTasks(player)` is called with the player as the leader, it checks if the player equals the leader (true), so it assigns `FollowLeaderAnyMeans` — but that doesn't make sense for the leader itself. This suggests the `DefaultPedTaskPairs` collection might only contain entries for gang members, not the leader, so the leader's task assignment happens through a different path entirely. I'm seeing a contradiction between what I thought I knew and what the actual source code shows. The allocator filters to only process the specific ped passed in, and when that ped is the leader, it assigns them a FollowLeaderAnyMeans task—which seems backwards since the leader shouldn't be following themselves. This suggests either my understanding of the flow is wrong, or there's something unusual about how default tasks are being set up for group leaders.

2026-03-15T15:51:15.0904721Z 
2026-03-15T15:51:15.0905028Z I'm iterating through group members and updating task pair references...
2026-03-15T15:51:15.0905513Z 
2026-03-15T15:51:15.0906170Z When the member list changes, `ComputeDefaultTasks(nullptr)` gets triggered, which then calls `AllocateDefaultTasks(m_pPedGroup, nullptr)` to reallocate default tasks for all members in their current slots.
2026-03-15T15:51:15.0906919Z 
2026-03-15T15:51:15.0908957Z The key insight is that when `ped` is `nullptr`, the condition `if (ped && tp.Ped != ped)` evaluates to false, so no pairs get skipped—all members are processed. Since `ped == nullptr` doesn't match the leader check, every member gets assigned `CTaskComplexWanderGang` instead of the follow task. But when this function is called with `ped = player` (the leader), it only processes the pair where `tp.Ped == player`, and since the leader check now passes, the correct follow task gets assigned.

2026-03-15T15:51:57.2930317Z copilot: Now I understand the full picture!
2026-03-15T15:51:57.2930900Z 
2026-03-15T15:51:57.2931219Z The member array has 8 slots. `LEADER_MEM_ID = 7` (the last slot). So:
2026-03-15T15:51:57.2931921Z - `m_members[0..6]` = followers (up to 7 followers)
2026-03-15T15:51:57.2932438Z - `m_members[7]` = leader
2026-03-15T15:51:57.2932683Z 
2026-03-15T15:51:57.2933099Z When `GetMembers(bIncludeLeader = true)` is called (default), it includes ALL 8 slots.
2026-03-15T15:51:57.2934277Z When `GetMembers(bIncludeLeader = false)` or `GetFollowers()` is called, it takes only the first 7 (excludes leader).
2026-03-15T15:51:57.2935340Z 
2026-03-15T15:51:57.2935500Z In `Process()`:
2026-03-15T15:51:57.2935703Z 
2026-03-15T15:51:57.2935708Z 
2026-03-15T15:51:57.2937373Z I'm iterating through all members including the leader, so the task pairs array gets populated with followers at indices 0-6 and the leader at index 7. Then in `AllocateDefaultTasks()`, I'm accessing the task pair at index 7 to get the leader's task.
2026-03-15T15:51:57.2938971Z 
2026-03-15T15:51:57.2941328Z Looking at the conditional logic more carefully now—when `ped == leader`, it assigns `CTaskComplexFollowLeaderAnyMeans` to that task slot, which means the leader gets a "follow leader" task assigned to themselves. The group intelligence's task resolution prioritizes script commands first, then primary tasks from event responses, and only falls back to default tasks if nothing else is set. When `TellGroupFollowWithRespect` is active, it sets primary tasks that completely override whatever default tasks were computed, so the default task system becomes irrelevant for the follower case.

2026-03-15T15:53:17.8824338Z copilot: Now I have everything I need. Let me read the actual grove_recruit_group.cpp and grove_recruit_ai.cpp to see exactly what the mod calls for GANG_SPAWN_AI_END:
2026-03-15T15:53:17.8827285Z 
2026-03-15T15:53:17.8827734Z copilot: Now I have the critical insight. Let me piece together what we know:
2026-03-15T15:53:17.8828318Z 
2026-03-15T15:53:17.8829184Z 1. **`SetDefaultTaskAllocatorType(4)`** sets the allocator to **SIT_IN_LEADER_CAR** (not FOLLOW_ANY_MEANS!). The mod uses `4` thinking it's FOLLOW_ANY_MEANS but:
2026-03-15T15:53:17.8830344Z    - 0 = FOLLOW_ANY_MEANS
2026-03-15T15:53:17.8830954Z    - 1 = FOLLOW_LIMITED
2026-03-15T15:53:17.8831310Z    - 2 = STAND_STILL
2026-03-15T15:53:17.8831642Z    - 3 = CHAT
2026-03-15T15:53:17.8832243Z    - 4 = SIT_IN_LEADER_CAR ← WRONG!
2026-03-15T15:53:17.8832646Z    
2026-03-15T15:53:17.8835832Z 2. The real follow behavior isn't coming from the default task allocator at all—it's being set through `TellGroupFollowWithRespect`, which bypasses the default system and directly assigns a PRIMARY task like `TASK_COMPLEX_GANG_FOLLOWER` or `TASK_GROUP_FOLLOW_LEADER_ANY_MEANS` to each member. So even though the allocator is misconfigured, the group still follows because this event handler is overriding it with the correct task.
2026-03-15T15:53:17.8838863Z 
2026-03-15T15:53:17.8841796Z 3. The player's own group uses a RANDOM allocator by default, and type 0 (FOLLOW_ANY_MEANS) is actually an unused task type that has a DebugBreak in its constructor—it's never called in normal gameplay. The current mod code sets type 4 (SIT_IN_LEADER_CAR), which would make recruits try to get into the player's car instead of following on foot.
2026-03-15T15:53:17.8843957Z 
2026-03-15T15:53:17.8844973Z 4. Type 1 (FOLLOW_LIMITED) is what I need to check—it assigns a different follow task that might be more appropriate for on-foot following behavior.
2026-03-15T15:53:17.8845915Z 
2026-03-15T15:53:17.8848210Z 5. The real issue is that the mod's approach of using `SetDefaultTaskAllocatorType` combined with `ComputeDefaultTasks` is fundamentally flawed because it's using the wrong allocator type, and even if corrected, it would still result in incorrect behavior like WanderGang for all group members. The actual follow mechanism should be using `TellGroupFollowWithRespect` instead.
2026-03-15T15:53:17.8850954Z 
2026-03-15T15:53:17.8854043Z 6. Looking at the runtime behavior, `TellGroupFollowWithRespect` is being called when recruits are added, but the GANG_JOIN_RESPOND task is getting overridden or interrupted, which is why the follow behavior breaks. The fallback should probably re-invoke `TellGroupFollowWithRespect` or `TellGroupToStartFollowingPlayer` to restore the follow state rather than trying to manipulate default tasks. riding it! When GANG_JOIN_RESPOND finishes, the recruit has STAND_STILL and the follow task is gone.
2026-03-15T15:53:17.8856961Z 
2026-03-15T15:53:17.8857098Z This suggests:
2026-03-15T15:53:17.8857981Z 1. `TellGroupFollowWithRespect` assigns the follow task correctly (slot[3] = GANG_FOLLOW_PRIMARY which is actually TASK_COMPLEX_BE_IN_GROUP = 243)
2026-03-15T15:53:17.8859398Z 2. GANG_JOIN_RESPOND (task 1219) runs in slot[2] as an event-response task and KILLS the follow task when it finishes
2026-03-15T15:53:17.8860521Z 3. The fix should be to RE-CALL `TellGroupFollowWithRespect` AFTER GANG_JOIN_RESPOND completes
2026-03-15T15:53:17.8861466Z 
2026-03-15T15:53:17.8864629Z From the log, the GANG_SPAWN_AI_END event fires at frame 0000721 when task 400 (ANIM) transitions to 203 (STAND_STILL). At this point, the mod re-emits follow via a cleanup and re-emission sequence, but FOLLOW_FALLBACK keeps failing. The real culprit is `bKeepTasksAfterCleanUp=1` — this flag is blocking the task system from properly clearing and reapplying tasks, so when `TellGroupFollowWithResp` tries to set the follow task, it can't override the existing state.
2026-03-15T15:53:17.8867354Z 
2026-03-15T15:53:17.8869914Z The stored memory indicates the fix: before calling `MakeThisPedJoinOurGroup`, set `bKeepTasksAfterCleanUp=0` and clear slot[2], then after success, call `GroupIntelComputeDefaultTasks` and restore the flag. But the issue is that `bKeepTasksAfterCleanUp=1` is preventing the follow task from being assigned after GANG_JOIN_RESPOND completes. I need to check the grove_recruit_ai.cpp code for GANG_SPAWN_AI_END to see how this is being handled.

2026-03-15T15:54:22.3625526Z

2026-03-15T15:54:22.3629352Z

2026-03-15T15:54:22.3634484Z 
2026-03-15T15:54:22.3635554Z Now looking at the allocator type issue: the code sets allocator type 4, which maps to SIT_IN_LEADER_CAR instead of the intended FOLLOW_ANY_MEANS (which is 0). This is clearly wrong—it's forcing recruits into the wrong behavior mode.
2026-03-15T15:54:22.3636619Z 
2026-03-15T15:54:22.3639366Z But there's a deeper problem here. Even if we corrected it to 0, the real issue is that SetDefaultTaskAllocator internally calls AllocateDefaultTasks with nullptr, which means it allocates tasks for all group members immediately, not just the leader. So everyone including the recruit would get WanderGang tasks assigned right away, which defeats the purpose of what the mod is trying to do. Calling `AllocateDefaultTasks` with nullptr causes all group members to default to WanderGang behavior, which defeats the purpose entirely. The real solution is to invoke `TellGroupFollowWithRespect` directly instead of manipulating the task allocator, since that function properly establishes the GANG_FOLLOWER task through the event system rather than through default task assignment.
2026-03-15T15:54:22.3642306Z 
2026-03-15T15:54:22.3643447Z Now I'm tracing through what happens when the allocator type is set to 4 (SIT_IN_LEADER_CAR) and `GroupIntelComputeDefaultTasks` runs with the player as the target—it flushes the leader's existing task and then calls the allocator's method, which checks if a leader exists before proceeding.
2026-03-15T15:54:22.3644473Z 
2026-03-15T15:54:22.3646002Z The allocator immediately checks if the leader has a vehicle, and if not, it returns without doing anything. So when the player is on foot, the function exits early and never assigns any tasks to the group members. That's why FOLLOW_FALLBACK ends up doing nothing useful—the allocator gets set to SIT_IN_LEADER_CAR, but since the player has no vehicle, it just bails out without allocating any meaningful tasks.
2026-03-15T15:54:22.3647365Z 
2026-03-15T15:54:22.3648292Z But TellGroupFollowWithRespect is being called both in GANG_SPAWN_AI_END and in the burst system, so there's something else preventing the recruit from actually following. I need to trace through what TellGroupFollowWithRespect actually does and why it's not working despite being called.
2026-03-15T15:54:22.3649323Z 
2026-03-15T15:54:22.3650243Z After a successful re-join, the system calls ComputeDefaultTasks with type=1 (FOLLOW_LIMITED), which assigns different tasks based on whether the ped is the leader or not—the leader gets a formation-following task while others get a wander task.
2026-03-15T15:54:22.3651303Z 
2026-03-15T15:54:22.3652870Z But wait, I'm seeing a logic issue here. When the player is the leader and we call ComputeDefaultTasks(player), the function iterates through pairs and only processes the one where tp.Ped equals the player. Then it checks if ped (the player) equals leader (also the player), which is true, so the leader would get assigned a FollowLeaderInFormation task that makes them follow themselves—that can't be right.
2026-03-15T15:54:22.3654266Z 
2026-03-15T15:54:22.3654495Z I think I've been misunderstanding how GetMembers() works in the Process function.
2026-03-15T15:54:22.3654821Z 
2026-03-15T15:54:22.3655988Z Examining the code more carefully, GetMembers() returns a filtered range where the enumerate index i corresponds to positions in that filtered sequence, not the original array. So if there's one member at array position 0 and the leader at position 7, GetMembers(true) would return them in sequence, but the indices would be 0 and 1 respectively in the enumeration.
2026-03-15T15:54:22.3657228Z 
2026-03-15T15:54:22.3658014Z When AllocateDefaultTasks is called with nullptr as the leader parameter, the comparison `ped == leader` always evaluates to false since nullptr never equals any actual ped, so every member gets assigned WanderGang regardless of the allocator type.
2026-03-15T15:54:22.3658887Z 
2026-03-15T15:54:22.3660208Z But when the player is passed as the leader in FOLLOW_LIMITED mode, only the player's slot gets processed and the condition `ped == leader` becomes true, which assigns FollowLeaderInFormation to the player—essentially telling the player to follow themselves, which seems like a bug or a misunderstanding of how the DefaultPedTaskPairs semantics work.
2026-03-15T15:54:22.3661828Z 
2026-03-15T15:54:22.3662857Z Let me reconsider this from scratch: GetDefaultTask is called for a specific ped as part of GetTaskMain, and m_DefaultPedTaskPairs stores the mapping between peds and their default tasks, so when looking up a task for a particular ped, it should find that ped's entry in the pairs array.
2026-03-15T15:54:22.3663847Z 
2026-03-15T15:54:22.3665092Z The real question is whether the engine actually calls GetTaskMain for group members at all, or if the group intelligence assigns tasks through a different mechanism. Looking at how Process() iterates through group members and updates the DefaultPedTaskPairs array, it seems like the tasks are being set directly on each ped's task manager rather than being retrieved through GetTaskMain.

2026-03-15T15:54:58.1429114Z 
2026-03-15T15:54:58.1430015Z copilot: Now I understand the full picture of how the group intelligence works. The `GetTaskMain(ped)` chain:
2026-03-15T15:54:58.1430751Z 
2026-03-15T15:54:58.1431345Z 1. `GetTaskScriptCommand(ped)` → from `m_ScriptCommandPedTaskPairs`
2026-03-15T15:54:58.1432063Z 2. `GetTask(ped, m_PedTaskPairs)` → event-response tasks (from TellGroupFollow)
2026-03-15T15:54:58.1432695Z 3. `GetTaskDefault(ped)` → from `m_DefaultPedTaskPairs`
2026-03-15T15:54:58.1433028Z 
2026-03-15T15:54:58.1434054Z But `GetTaskMain` is NOT called by the engine directly to get tasks to run. Instead, the ped's intelligence uses something like `CTaskManager::Process()` which runs the ped's currently assigned tasks. The group intelligence SETS tasks ON the ped via:
2026-03-15T15:54:58.1435103Z 
2026-03-15T15:54:58.1435108Z 
2026-03-15T15:54:58.1435463Z - `SetTask(ped, task, m_PedTaskPairs)` → sets to the ped's task manager PRIMARY slot
2026-03-15T15:54:58.1436177Z - The task in `m_DefaultPedTaskPairs` is used as fallback when creating next subtasks
2026-03-15T15:54:58.1436736Z 
2026-03-15T15:54:58.1439480Z I'm realizing the group intelligence tasks might actually be separate from the ped's CTaskManager—the `m_PedTaskPairs` etc. in CPedGroupIntelligence represent the intelligence's view of what tasks should be assigned, and they get applied to the ped's CTaskManager through some other mechanism. I need to find where `CTaskManager::SetTask` is called or how these tasks actually get transferred over.
2026-03-15T15:54:58.1441976Z 
2026-03-15T15:54:58.1444028Z Looking at the runtime logs, the core issue is obvious: the recruit stays locked in STAND_STILL (203) regardless of how many FOLLOW_FALLBACK cycles run or how many times TellGroupFollowWithRespect gets called. The current approach of using `SetDefaultTaskAllocatorType(4)` with `ComputeDefaultTasks(player)` isn't working because type 4 is SIT_IN_LEADER_CAR (wrong type), and even if it were correct, it only affects the leader's default task pair rather than actually driving the follow behavior. The default task is just a fallback, not the real mechanism that should be forcing the follow action.
2026-03-15T15:54:58.1446142Z 
2026-03-15T15:54:58.1448299Z The real solution is either to call `TellGroupFollowWithRespect` repeatedly, or more importantly, figure out what's preventing the follow task from being assigned once GANG_JOIN_RESPOND (1219) finishes. Looking at the rescan data, I see `bKeepTasksAfterCleanUp=1` with GANG_JOIN_RESPOND still active in slot[2], and there's a comment about ClearTaskEventResponse clearing slots to allow new tasks through—that's likely the key to understanding what's blocking the transition.
2026-03-15T15:54:58.1450076Z 
2026-03-15T15:54:58.1452055Z Now I'm checking whether the mod is correctly calling ClearTaskEventResponse before TellGroupFollowWithRespect, and I'm also noticing something odd with the GANG_SPAWN_AI_END check. The frame data shows the task changing from 400 to 203 (STAND_STILL), so the condition should be triggering at frame 721 when `g_prevRecruitTaskId` gets set to 400.
2026-03-15T15:54:58.1453780Z 
2026-03-15T15:54:58.1457708Z At that point the code clears the task event response, calls TellGroupFollowWithRespect, and resets the follow timers. Looking at the stored memory fact about the recruit freeze fix, I'm realizing that ComputeDefaultTasks might work differently than I thought — maybe the DEFAULT task pair for the LEADER actually determines what gets assigned to group members, not the LEADER itself. 2026-03-15T15:55:14.3066410Z copilot: This is extremely important. `TellGroupToStartFollowingPlayer` does NOT directly assign tasks to group members! Instead, it:
2026-03-15T15:55:14.3067265Z 
2026-03-15T15:55:14.3067459Z 1. Checks `m_bGroupAlwaysFollow` and `m_bGroupNeverFollow` flags
2026-03-15T15:55:14.3068027Z 2. Sets `group.m_bMembersEnterLeadersVehicle = arg0`
2026-03-15T15:55:14.3068909Z 3. Calls `groupIntel.SetDefaultTaskAllocatorType(RANDOM)` ← Sets to RANDOM!
2026-03-15T15:55:14.3069663Z 4. If `arg0 = true`: Creates and adds a `CEventPlayerCommandToGroup` event to the group intelligence
2026-03-15T15:55:14.3070069Z 
2026-03-15T15:55:14.3070328Z So `TellGroupToStartFollowingPlayer(arg0=true, arg1, arg2)`:
2026-03-15T15:55:14.3070890Z 
2026-03-15T15:55:14.3070913Z 
2026-03-15T15:55:14.3071018Z - Sets allocator to RANDOM
2026-03-15T15:55:14.3071452Z - Fires a `PLAYER_GROUP_COMMAND_GATHER` event (or whatever `ComputeResponseTaskType` decides)
2026-03-15T15:55:14.3071957Z 
2026-03-15T15:55:14.3072940Z The actual follow task assignment happens through the EVENT SYSTEM, not through direct task assignment! Now I need to check what the mod's `TellGroupFollowWithRespect` does when it calls this function, looking at grove_recruit_shared.h to understand the full flow.

2026-03-15T15:56:18.6396607Z 
2026-03-15T15:56:18.6397101Z copilot: Now I understand the full picture:
2026-03-15T15:56:18.6397514Z 
2026-03-15T15:56:18.6398224Z `TellGroupToStartFollowingPlayer(aggressive=false, arg1=false, arg2=false)` is called. From the gta-reversed implementation:
2026-03-15T15:56:18.6398897Z 
2026-03-15T15:56:18.6398972Z ```cpp
2026-03-15T15:56:18.6400080Z void CPlayerPed::TellGroupToStartFollowingPlayer(bool arg0, bool arg1, bool arg2) {
2026-03-15T15:56:18.6404835Z     if (GetPlayerData()->m_bGroupAlwaysFollow && !arg0)
2026-03-15T15:56:18.6406527Z         return;  // ← RETURNS EARLY if m_bGroupAlwaysFollow=true and arg0=false!
2026-03-15T15:56:18.6407650Z     if (GetPlayerData()->m_bGroupNeverFollow && arg0)
2026-03-15T15:56:18.6408170Z         return;
2026-03-15T15:56:18.6408470Z ```
2026-03-15T15:56:18.6408626Z 
2026-03-15T15:56:18.6410805Z This is the critical bug—when `aggressive=false` and `m_bGroupAlwaysFollow=true`, the function exits early without executing anything. But checking the mod's ON_FOOT case, `TellGroupFollowWithRespect(player, g_aggressive, true)` passes `g_aggressive`, which the log shows as `aggr=1` (true), so `arg0=true` and the early return shouldn't trigger.
2026-03-15T15:56:18.6412973Z 
2026-03-15T15:56:18.6415384Z Looking at the condition more carefully: `m_bGroupAlwaysFollow && !arg0` evaluates to `true && false` = `false`, so it doesn't return early. Then examining the spawn sequence in the log, after GANG_SPAWN_AI_END completes and TellGroupFollowWithRespect is called with `aggressive=true`, the function should proceed through the flag checks and set the follow state, but the follow assignment never actually happens.
2026-03-15T15:56:18.6417198Z 
2026-03-15T15:56:18.6419968Z The real issue is that when `arg0=true` (aggressive mode), the code sets `m_bMembersEnterLeadersVehicle = true` and fires a GATHER event—which is actually the "enter vehicle" command meant for when the player wants the group to get in the car. This is wrong for on-foot following. When `arg0=false` (non-aggressive), the GATHER event wouldn't fire at all, so the follow behavior gets set up differently.
2026-03-15T15:56:18.6422327Z 
2026-03-15T15:56:18.6427074Z I need to look at what `m_bMembersEnterLeadersVehicle` actually controls and what the event firing logic really does to understand if this is a bug or if I'm misreading the intent. So when `arg0=false`, the allocator defaults to RANDOM and `ComputeDefaultTasks(nullptr)` assigns WanderGang to everyone, effectively stopping followers. When `arg0=true`, it fires a GATHER event that should assign the follow task via `ComputeResponseTaskType`. The mod is calling this with `true`, which fires the event, but the recruit still ends up with STAND_STILL instead of following—so I need to trace what `ComputeResponseTaskType` actually returns for player groups versus gang followers.
2026-03-15T15:56:18.6430892Z 
2026-03-15T15:56:18.6433305Z Looking at the mod's call with `arg2=false`, there's a guard that returns early if there are no members excluding the leader, but the recruit is clearly in the group, so that check passes. The function executes fully, but the GATHER event isn't resulting in a follow task. This might come down to the `m_acquaintance.m_nRespect` value—there's a comment in AddRecruitToGroup that hints the Respects check might be blocking the task assignment.
2026-03-15T15:56:18.6435904Z 
2026-03-15T15:56:18.6437791Z The mod sets the respect bit when adding the recruit to the group, but maybe something in the GANG_JOIN_RESPOND sequence clears it. The static STAT_RESPECT value of 1000 in the logs isn't the same as the actual `m_acquaintance.m_nRespect` field, so I need to check what that value actually is at the point where CreateFirstSubTask runs.
2026-03-15T15:56:18.6439009Z 
2026-03-15T15:56:18.6440128Z Looking at the follow flags more carefully—`m_bGroupAlwaysFollow` being false doesn't cause an early return when the recruit is aggressive, but `m_bGroupNeverFollow` being true would trigger an early return, and the mod never sets this to false, which could be blocking the follow task entirely.
2026-03-15T15:56:18.6441394Z 
2026-03-15T15:56:18.6442418Z Then there's the backup case where `AddFollower` is used instead of `MakeThisPedJoinOurGroup`—if that initial join failed, the ped might not be properly registered in the group intelligence system, which could prevent the default task pairs from being set up correctly.
2026-03-15T15:56:18.6443579Z 
2026-03-15T15:56:18.6444540Z Looking at the logs, the initial join attempt failed at frame 601, so the ped was added via the fallback method. But then at frame 720, a re-join attempt succeeded with `MakeThisPedJoinOurGroup`, which means the ped finally got properly registered in the group at that point.
2026-03-15T15:56:18.6445472Z 
2026-03-15T15:56:18.6447301Z After the successful re-join, both the mod's group.cpp code and the GANG_SPAWN_AI_END event are calling `TellGroupFollowWithRespect` with aggressive=true, yet the follow behavior still isn't working. 2026-03-15T15:57:53.7976563Z copilot: **EUREKA!** Now I understand the FULL picture!
2026-03-15T15:57:53.7977009Z 
2026-03-15T15:57:53.7977419Z `GetTaskMain(ped)` is called from `TASK_COMPLEX_BE_IN_GROUP` (task 243)! This is the KEY:
2026-03-15T15:57:53.7978060Z 
2026-03-15T15:57:53.7978233Z - Task 243 = `TASK_COMPLEX_BE_IN_GROUP`
2026-03-15T15:57:53.7979138Z - This task runs in slot[3] (primary group task slot)  
2026-03-15T15:57:53.7979980Z - Inside it calls `intel.GetTaskMain(ped)` which returns the group intelligence's main task
2026-03-15T15:57:53.7982047Z - `GetTaskMain(ped)` returns: `ScriptCommandTask || PedTaskPairTask || DefaultTask`
2026-03-15T15:57:53.7982697Z 
2026-03-15T15:57:53.7982843Z So the chain is:
2026-03-15T15:57:53.7983075Z 
2026-03-15T15:57:53.7983082Z 
2026-03-15T15:57:53.7983324Z 1. Recruit has `TASK_COMPLEX_BE_IN_GROUP` in slot[3]
2026-03-15T15:57:53.7984187Z 2. Each frame, this task queries the group intelligence for its main task via `GetTaskMain(ped)`
2026-03-15T15:57:53.7986107Z 3. The group intelligence returns whatever task is stored in `m_PedTaskPairs[recruit]` — which gets set by the GATHER event from `TellGroupToStartFollowingPlayer`
2026-03-15T15:57:53.7987570Z 4. That event assigns a `CTaskComplexSeekEntity` task that directs the recruit toward the player
2026-03-15T15:57:53.7988002Z 
2026-03-15T15:57:53.7988462Z For the recruit to follow the player, slot[3] must remain occupied by the group task so it can continuously pull the seek task from the group intelligence.
2026-03-15T15:57:53.7989012Z 
2026-03-15T15:57:53.7994631Z But looking at the actual log data, slot[3] shows `NO_TASK(-1)` at frame 720 and appears to be `NO_TASK` again at frame 840. The recruit never has the group task in slot[3] at all, which explains why it's not following — there's nothing there to query the group intelligence for movement instructions. I'm realizing the core problem: `TASK_COMPLEX_BE_IN_GROUP` isn't being assigned to the recruit even after the successful re-join at frame 720. Looking at how `TaskComplexBeInGroup` works, it retrieves the main task from the group's intelligence system, so the actual task shown would be whatever subtask the group assigns rather than the wrapper itself. This means the task dump might be showing the underlying subtask instead of the complex task container, which could explain why I'm seeing `NO_TASK` in that slot. Looking at the sequence of opcodes in the CLEO version, I can see how the group follow system works—it locks members, adds the ped to the group, sets respect, initiates the follow tasks, and then uses a direct follow task assignment to bypass the normal group intelligence. The issue is that when the plugin-sdk version calls `MakeThisPedJoinOurGroup`, it should be creating a `TASK_COMPLEX_BE_IN_GROUP` task in slot[3], but the frame 720 log shows slot[3] is empty, meaning the task never got assigned—though I'm not entirely certain that's the correct slot to check.
2026-03-15T15:57:53.7999410Z 
2026-03-15T15:57:53.8002207Z Now I'm reviewing the actual slot mapping in the CTaskManager to figure out where `BE_IN_GROUP` should end up, since the log shows `STAND_STILL` in slot[4] instead. If slot[3] is truly `PRIMARY_DEFAULT`, that's where the group task should be, but something's preventing it from getting there. I see the issue now—the code is setting `bKeepTasksAfterCleanUp` to 0 before joining the group to clear out the old task slots, then calling `MakeThisPedJoinOurGroup`, and afterward restoring the flag to 1 and recomputing default tasks. But looking at the log at frame 720 when the re-join happens, the slot assignments aren't being restored properly after that process completes.

2026-03-15T15:58:11.6133285Z 1. It's placed in `TASK_PRIMARY_PRIMARY` (slot[3] or actually the "primary" slot, which is index 3 = DEFAULT slot)
2026-03-15T15:58:11.6134372Z 2. Each frame it calls `intel.GetTaskMain(ped)` to get the current group intelligence task
2026-03-15T15:58:11.6135482Z 3. If the group has a task (from TellGroupToStartFollowingPlayer/GATHER event), BE_IN_GROUP runs it
2026-03-15T15:58:11.6136453Z 4. If no task, BE_IN_GROUP returns nullptr (ped stands still)
2026-03-15T15:58:11.6136866Z 
2026-03-15T15:58:11.6136873Z 
2026-03-15T15:58:11.6137674Z 5. The code is cloning BE_IN_GROUP from the primary task slot to check its state, confirming it's consistently placed at that index across the codebase.

2026-03-15T16:00:09.4460309Z copilot: Now I understand the FULL mechanism:
2026-03-15T16:00:09.4460916Z 
2026-03-15T16:00:09.4461072Z From `FlushImmediately`:
2026-03-15T16:00:09.4461442Z ```cpp
2026-03-15T16:00:09.4461763Z // Restore group primary task
2026-03-15T16:00:09.4462514Z if (tComplexBeInGroupClone) {    pedGroup->GetIntelligence().ComputeDefaultTasks(m_pPed);
2026-03-15T16:00:09.4463510Z     m_TaskMgr.SetTask(tComplexBeInGroupClone, TASK_PRIMARY_PRIMARY, false);
2026-03-15T16:00:09.4464162Z }
2026-03-15T16:00:09.4464423Z ```
2026-03-15T16:00:09.4464581Z 
2026-03-15T16:00:09.4465483Z BE_IN_GROUP (243) is in `TASK_PRIMARY_PRIMARY`. When a ped undergoes `FlushImmediately` (e.g., from a gang spawn, or when hit), the BE_IN_GROUP task is preserved and restored.
2026-03-15T16:00:09.4466580Z 
2026-03-15T16:00:09.4466585Z 
2026-03-15T16:00:09.4468847Z But `AddMember` doesn't assign BE_IN_GROUP at all—it only updates the member list and changes the decision maker type. So the assignment must happen when the group's `Process()` detects the member list changed and calls `ComputeDefaultTasks(nullptr)`, which then assigns the task to the new member.
2026-03-15T16:00:09.4470919Z 
2026-03-15T16:00:09.4472425Z Wait, I'm confusing things. The DEFAULT task is what BE_IN_GROUP *runs*, not BE_IN_GROUP itself. So BE_IN_GROUP (task 243) has to be assigned to the ped's primary task slot by something else entirely. Let me trace through `MakeThisPedJoinOurGroup` to see where that actually happens.
2026-03-15T16:00:09.4474145Z 
2026-03-15T16:00:09.4476003Z Looking at the group membership code, `AddMember` only sets the decision maker type, it doesn't assign BE_IN_GROUP. But `MakeThisPedJoinOurGroup` does something more involved than just calling `AddMember`. This creates a situation where the group member appears to finish their task immediately and loop back, potentially getting stuck in a completion cycle unless the group intelligence eventually provides a valid main task.

2026-03-15T16:08:41.7893592Z       4. **Wrong task names** — 30+ wrong names in GetTaskName (e.g., 900=GO_TO_POINT not REACT_TO_CMD, 902=ACHIEVE_HEADING not FLEE, 207=FALL not WALK_TO_POINT, etc.)

2026-03-15T16:18:01.5300801Z copilot: ## Summary of Changes
2026-03-15T16:18:01.5301059Z 
2026-03-15T16:18:01.5301216Z ### Root Cause Found (via gta-reversed source)
2026-03-15T16:18:01.5301455Z 
2026-03-15T16:18:01.5301682Z The recruit was stuck in `STAND_STILL` forever due to **3 compounding bugs**:
2026-03-15T16:18:01.5302021Z 
2026-03-15T16:18:01.5302104Z ---
2026-03-15T16:18:01.5302213Z 
2026-03-15T16:18:01.5302650Z ### Bug 1 — CRITICAL: BE_IN_GROUP(243) never assigned to slot[3]
2026-03-15T16:18:01.5302933Z 
2026-03-15T16:18:01.5303131Z **How follow actually works** (from `TaskComplexBeInGroup.cpp`):
2026-03-15T16:18:01.5303628Z - `TASK_COMPLEX_BE_IN_GROUP` must be in `TASK_PRIMARY_PRIMARY` (slot[3])
2026-03-15T16:18:01.5305181Z - Each frame: `BeInGroup::ControlSubTask` → `MonitorMainGroupTask` → `intel.GetTaskMain(recruit)` → returns `CTaskComplexSeekEntity` (placed by `ComputeResponseGather` when `TellGroupToStartFollowingPlayer(true)` fires GATHER event) → recruit walks toward player
2026-03-15T16:18:01.5307526Z - **Without BE_IN_GROUP in slot[3]**: `GetTaskMain(recruit)` is never called, GATHER events are silently ignored, recruit stays STAND_STILL forever
2026-03-15T16:18:01.5308290Z 
2026-03-15T16:18:01.5311120Z **Fix**: Added `EnsureBeInGroup(recruit, groupId)` in `grove_recruit_shared.h` — creates `CTaskComplexBeInGroup` (constructor @`0x632E50`, size `0x28` bytes) via `CTaskManager::SetTask` to `TASK_PRIMARY_PRIMARY` if not present. Called after every successful `MakeThisPedJoinOurGroup` and in `GANG_SPAWN_ANIM_END`/`FOLLOW_FALLBACK`.
2026-03-15T16:18:01.5313232Z 
2026-03-15T16:18:01.5313367Z ---
2026-03-15T16:18:01.5313625Z 
2026-03-15T16:18:01.5313922Z ### Bug 2 — Wrong `followOk` task IDs
2026-03-15T16:18:01.5314247Z 
2026-03-15T16:18:01.5314566Z - `207` = `TASK_SIMPLE_FALL` — **NOT a follow task** (was wrongly labeled WALK_TO_POINT)
2026-03-15T16:18:01.5315530Z - `208` = `TASK_COMPLEX_FALL_AND_GET_UP` — **NOT a follow task** (was wrongly labeled FOLLOW_LEADER_FORM)
2026-03-15T16:18:01.5316171Z - Added `913` = `TASK_COMPLEX_FOLLOW_LEADER_IN_FORMATION` (valid follow state, was missing)
2026-03-15T16:18:01.5316527Z 
2026-03-15T16:18:01.5316603Z ---
2026-03-15T16:18:01.5316714Z 
2026-03-15T16:18:01.5316850Z ### Bug 3 — Wrong FOLLOW_FALLBACK
2026-03-15T16:18:01.5317026Z 
2026-03-15T16:18:01.5317309Z - `SetDefaultTaskAllocatorType(4)` = `SIT_IN_LEADER_CAR` (NOT FollowLeaderAnyMeans as assumed!)
2026-03-15T16:18:01.5318114Z - `ComputeDefaultTasks(player)` only affects the **leader's** default task pair — does nothing for the recruit
2026-03-15T16:18:01.5319122Z - **Fix**: Fallback now calls `EnsureBeInGroup + TellGroupFollowWithRespect` which fires GATHER event → `SeekEntity` consumed by `BE_IN_GROUP`

2026-03-15T16:18:20.9598378Z Recruit permanently frozen in `STAND_STILL` after spawn due to three compounding bugs discovered via `gta-reversed` source analysis.
2026-03-15T16:18:20.9599296Z 
2026-03-15T16:18:20.9599497Z ## Root Cause: BE_IN_GROUP never in slot[3]
2026-03-15T16:18:20.9599849Z 
2026-03-15T16:18:20.9600380Z `TASK_COMPLEX_BE_IN_GROUP` (243) must occupy `TASK_PRIMARY_PRIMARY` (slot[3]) for the follow chain to function:
2026-03-15T16:18:20.9601386Z 
2026-03-15T16:18:20.9601509Z ```
2026-03-15T16:18:20.9601900Z TellGroupToStartFollowingPlayer(aggressive=true)
2026-03-15T16:18:20.9602844Z   → GATHER event → ComputeResponseGather → SeekEntity in m_PedTaskPairs[recruit]
2026-03-15T16:18:20.9605872Z   → BeInGroup::ControlSubTask → MonitorMainGroupTask → GetTaskMain(recruit)
2026-03-15T16:18:20.9606774Z   → returns SeekEntity → recruit walks toward player
2026-03-15T16:18:20.9607289Z ```
2026-03-15T16:18:20.9607475Z 
2026-03-15T16:18:20.9608651Z Without BE_IN_GROUP in slot[3], `GetTaskMain(recruit)` is never called — GATHER events are silently ignored regardless of how many times `TellGroupFollowWithRespect` fires.
2026-03-15T16:18:20.9609640Z 
2026-03-15T16:18:20.9610376Z `MakeThisPedJoinOurGroup` silently fails to assign BE_IN_GROUP under spawn conditions (residual anim tasks, `bKeepTasksAfterCleanUp`, etc.).
2026-03-15T16:18:20.9611442Z 
2026-03-15T16:18:20.9613487Z **Fix**: Added `EnsureBeInGroup(recruit, groupId)` in `grove_recruit_shared.h` — allocates `CTaskComplexBeInGroup` (ctor `@0x632E50`, size `0x28`) and calls `CTaskManager::SetTask` to `TASK_PRIMARY_PRIMARY` directly. Called after every successful join, after `TASK_SIMPLE_ANIM(400)` ends, and in `FOLLOW_FALLBACK`.
2026-03-15T16:18:20.9615218Z 
2026-03-15T16:18:20.9615359Z ## Wrong `followOk` task IDs
2026-03-15T16:18:20.9615625Z 
2026-03-15T16:18:20.9616083Z - `207` = `TASK_SIMPLE_FALL` — not a follow task (was mislabeled `WALK_TO_POINT`)
2026-03-15T16:18:20.9617472Z - `208` = `TASK_COMPLEX_FALL_AND_GET_UP` — not a follow task (was mislabeled `FOLLOW_LEADER_FORM`)
2026-03-15T16:18:20.9618401Z - Added `913` = `TASK_COMPLEX_FOLLOW_LEADER_IN_FORMATION` (valid follow state, was absent)
2026-03-15T16:18:20.9618928Z 
2026-03-15T16:18:20.9619238Z ## Wrong FOLLOW_FALLBACK
2026-03-15T16:18:20.9619462Z 
2026-03-15T16:18:20.9621445Z `SetDefaultTaskAllocatorType(4)` = `SIT_IN_LEADER_CAR` (not `FOLLOW_ANY_MEANS` as assumed). `ComputeDefaultTasks(player)` only updates the leader's `m_DefaultPedTaskPairs` slot — has zero effect on the recruit. Replaced with `EnsureBeInGroup + TellGroupFollowWithRespect`.
2026-03-15T16:18:20.9623158Z 
2026-03-15T16:18:20.9623328Z ## 30+ wrong task names in `GetTaskName()`
2026-03-15T16:18:20.9623644Z 
2026-03-15T16:18:20.9626603Z Corrected from `gta-reversed` `eTaskType` enum — critical entries: `207→SIMPLE_FALL`, `208→COMPLEX_FALL_AND_GET_UP`, `243→BE_IN_GROUP`, `400→SIMPLE_ANIM`, `900→SIMPLE_GO_TO_POINT`, `902→SIMPLE_ACHIEVE_HEADING`, `913` added, `1219→COMPLEX_GANG_JOIN_RESPOND`, `700↔701` swapped (`PASSENGER`/`DRIVER`). Also corrected allocator type enum documentation (1=`FOLLOW_LIMITED`, 4=`SIT_IN_LEADER_CAR`, 5=`RANDOM`) and `ComputeDefaultTasks` contract comments.
2026-03-15T16:18:20.9629357Z </pr_description>
